class="articleHeaderDropzone4" data-pb-dropzone="articleHeaderDropzone4"><div class="articleRightsPermissionsLink"><a href="/servlet/linkout?type=rightslink&amp;url=startPage%3D36902%26pageCount%3D8%26copyright%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26author%3DQiu-Li%2BNing%252C%2BBao-Hua%2BHou%252C%2BYing-Ying%2BWang%252C%2Bet%2Bal%26orderBeanReset%3Dtrue%26imprint%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26volumeNum%3D10%26issueNum%3D43%26contentID%3Dacsami.8b11103%26title%3DHierarchical%2BGeP5%252FCarbon%2BNanocomposite%2Bwith%2BDual-Carbon%2BConductive%2BNetwork%2Bas%2BPromising%2BAnode%2BMaterial%2Bfor%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26numPages%3D8%26pa%3D%26issn%3D1944-8244%26publisherName%3Dacs%26publication%3Daamick%26rpt%3Dn%26endPage%3D36909%26publicationDate%3DOctober%2B2018" data-id="article_rights_permissions">Request reuse permissions</a></div></div></div></div></div><div class="article_header-metrics-dropzone" data-pb-dropzone="article_header-metrics-dropzone"><!-- Empty dropzone --></div></div></div></div><div class="article_abstract"><div class="article_abstract-title" id="Abstract" tabindex="0"><h2>Abstract</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div><div class="article_abstract-content hlFld-Abstract" id="abstractBox" property="description"><figure id="_i1" data-index="0" class="article__inlineFigure article_abstract-img"><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img class="inline-fig internalNav" src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11103/asset/images/medium/am-2018-111039_0008.gif" alt="" id="tgr1" property="image" style="width:405px; height:275px"></button><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11103/asset/images/large/am-2018-111039_0008.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.8b11103&amp;id=_i1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><p class="articleBody_abstractText">Due to the Earth’s scarcity of lithium, replacing lithium with earth-abundant and low-cost sodium for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) has recently become a promising substitute for lithium-ion batteries. However, the shortage of appropriate anode materials limits the development of SIBs. Here, a dual-carbon conductive network enhanced GeP<sub>5</sub> (GeP<sub>5</sub>/acetylene black/partially reduced graphene oxide sheets (GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO)) composite is successfully prepared by a facile ball milling method. The dual-carbon network not only provides more transport pathways for electrons but also relaxes the huge volume change of the electrode material during the charge/discharge process. Compared with only AB- or GO-modified GeP<sub>5</sub> (GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB or GeP<sub>5</sub>/GO) composite, the GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO composite shows a superior sodium storage performance with an excellent rate and cycle performance. It delivers a high reversible capacity of 597.5 and 175 mAh/g at the current density of 0.1 and 5.0 A/g, respectively. Furthermore, at the current density of 0.5 A/g, the GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO composite shows the reversible capacity of 400 mAh/g after 50 cycles with a little capacity attenuation. All above results prove that the GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO composite has a good prospect of application as an anode material for SIBs.</p></div><div class="article__cc-license"><div class="article__cc-license__body"><p class="article__cc-license__para">This publication is licensed under the terms of your
                            institutional subscription.
                            <a href="/servlet/linkout?type=rightslink&amp;url=startPage%3D36902%26pageCount%3D8%26copyright%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26author%3DQiu-Li%2BNing%252C%2BBao-Hua%2BHou%252C%2BYing-Ying%2BWang%252C%2Bet%2Bal%26orderBeanReset%3Dtrue%26imprint%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26volumeNum%3D10%26issueNum%3D43%26contentID%3Dacsami.8b11103%26title%3DHierarchical%2BGeP5%252FCarbon%2BNanocomposite%2Bwith%2BDual-Carbon%2BConductive%2BNetwork%2Bas%2BPromising%2BAnode%2BMaterial%2Bfor%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26numPages%3D8%26pa%3D%26issn%3D1944-8244%26publisherName%3Dacs%26publication%3Daamick%26rpt%3Dn%26endPage%3D36909%26publicationDate%3DOctober%2B2018" class="link--bold">Request reuse permissions.</a></p></div></div><span class="hidden" property="publisher">ACS Publications</span><div class="article_header-article-copyright">Copyright © 2018 American Chemical Society</div><div class="article_header-footer-right"><div class="articleHeaderDropzone7" data-pb-dropzone="articleHeaderDropzone7"><div class="article__tags article__tags--subjects"><div class="article__tags__container"><header class="article__tags__header"><h3 class="article__tags__heading">Subjects</h3><div tabindex="0" class="article__tags__tooltip"><div aria-describedby="tooltip-subjects" class="article__tags__icon"><i class="icon-info-circle-outline"></i><span class="sr-only">what are subjects</span></div><p id="tooltip-subjects" role="tooltip" class="article__tags__diff">Article subjects are automatically applied from the ACS Subject Taxonomy and describe the scientific concepts and themes of the article.</p></div></header><ul class="article__tags__list"><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291442&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Anode materials" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Anode%20materials" class="article__tags__link">Anode materials</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291331&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Composites" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Composites" class="article__tags__link">Composites</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291371&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Electrodes" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Electrodes" class="article__tags__link">Electrodes</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=292506&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Materials" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Materials" class="article__tags__link">Materials</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=290920&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Nanoparticles" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Nanoparticles" class="article__tags__link">Nanoparticles</a></li></ul></div></div></div></div><div class="article__tags article__tags--keywords hlFld-Abstract"><div class="article__tags__container"><header class="article__tags__header"><h3 class="article__tags__heading">Keywords</h3><div class="article__tags__tooltip" tabindex="0"><div class="article__tags__icon" aria-describedby="tooltip-keywords"><i class="icon-info-circle-outline"></i><span class="sr-only">what are keywords</span></div><p class="article__tags__diff" id="tooltip-keywords" role="tooltip">
                        Article keywords are supplied by the authors and highlight key terms and topics
                        of the paper.
                    </p></div></header><ul class="article__tags__list"><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Sodium-ion+Batteries&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_sodium-ion%20batteries">sodium-ion batteries</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Anode+Material&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_anode%20material">anode material</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Gep5&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_GeP5">GeP<sub>5</sub></a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Carbon+Conductive+Network&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_carbon%20conductive%20network">carbon conductive network</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Composite&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_composite">composite</a></li></ul></div></div></div><div class="article_content"><div class="article_content-table hlFld-FullText"><div class="article_content-row"><div class="article_content-left" property="articleBody" style="width: 384px;"><div id="sec1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i2">1.  Introduction</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p">In the last decade, lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) as the main power sources for portable electronic devices, are gradually applied in large-scale products, such as hybrid vehicles, electric vehicles, and energy storage systems. However, ever-increasing demand of LIBs results in the shortage and fancy price of lithium resources. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref1 ref2 ref3 ref4 ref5 ref6'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref1 ref2 ref3 ref4 ref5 ref6" aria-label="reference 1 to 6">(1−6)</a> On the contrary, with the chemical properties similar to those of lithium, sodium is cheaper and more earth-abundant. Therefore, sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered as the promising alternative to LIBs. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref1 ref7 ref8 ref9 ref10 ref11'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref1 ref7 ref8 ref9 ref10 ref11" aria-label="reference 1 and 7 to 11">(1,7−11)</a> However, SIBs show relatively low specific capacity and poor rate capability and cycling stability than those of LIBs. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref7 ref12 ref13 ref14'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref7 ref12 ref13 ref14" aria-label="reference 7 and 12 to 14">(7,12−14)</a> The larger ion radius (1.02 Å for Na<sup>+</sup> vs 0.76 Å for Li<sup>+</sup>) results in the sluggish electrochemical reaction kinetics and huge volume change of the electrode materials during the sodiation/desodiation progress. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref15 ref16'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref15 ref16" aria-label="reference 15 and 16">(15,16)</a> Meanwhile the graphite anode, which is well-developed in LIBs is not suitable for SIBs. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref17 ref18 ref19'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref17 ref18 ref19" aria-label="reference 17 to 19">(17−19)</a> Therefore, it is highly desired to develop new anode materials for SIBs with high specific capacity and excellent cycling performance.</div><div class="NLM_p">In recent years, alloy-type materials (e.g., Sn-based materials, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref20 ref21 ref22 ref23'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref20 ref21 ref22 ref23" aria-label="reference 20 to 23">(20−23)</a> Sb-based materials, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref24 ref25 ref26'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref24 ref25 ref26" aria-label="reference 24 to 26">(24−26)</a> Si-based materials, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref27 ref28'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref27 ref28" aria-label="reference 27 and 28">(27,28)</a> Ge-based materials, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref29 ref30 ref31'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref29 ref30 ref31" aria-label="reference 29 to 31">(29−31)</a> P-based materials <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32 ref33 ref34'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref32 ref33 ref34" aria-label="reference 32 to 34">(32−34)</a>) have attracted wide attention because of their high theoretical specific capacity. However, these electrode materials suffer from the huge volume expansion during the alloying reaction, which causes a serious electrode pulverization and rapid capacity fade. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref1'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref1" aria-label="reference 1">(1)</a> So far, two available strategies, designing nanostructures and introducing conductive carbon (e.g., acetylene black, graphene), are used to accelerate the kinetics of the reaction and achieve stability of the alloy-type anode materials. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref1 ref20 ref28 ref29 ref35 ref36'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref1 ref20 ref28 ref29 ref35 ref36" aria-label="reference 1, 20, 28, 29, 35 and 36">(1,20,28,29,35,36)</a> Several studies have corroborated that nanosized Si shows sodium storage performance, but Si was not suitable as an anode material for SIBs due to low electrochemical activity. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref27 ref28 ref37 ref38 ref39'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref27 ref28 ref37 ref38 ref39" aria-label="reference 27, 28 and 37 to 39">(27,28,37−39)</a> On the contrary, Sn and Sb, showing a high theoretical specific capacity of 847 (Na<sub>15</sub>Sn<sub>4</sub>) and 660 mAh/g (Na<sub>3</sub>Sb), are extensively studied for SIBs. But the huge volume change leads to the electrode pulverization during sodiation/desodiation progress, consequently losing electrical contact with the current collector, causing capacity decay, and hindering the application as an SIB anode material. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref13 ref40'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref13 ref40" aria-label="reference 13 and 40">(13,40)</a></div><div class="NLM_p">Recently, phosphorus (P) has attracted much attention due to its high theoretical specific capacity (<i>w</i> ≈ 2600 mAh/g) and low cost. Zhou et al. reported hollow nanospheres with porous shells, which revealed great rate and cycle performance. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref33'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref33" aria-label="reference 33">(33)</a> Liu et al. developed a method to deposit red phosphorus nanodots densely and uniformly onto reduced graphene oxide sheets (P@RGO). The P@RGO flexible anode delivered a capacity of 914 mAh/g after 300 cycles at the current density of 1593.9 mA/g. Although some studies have been carried out about the P-based materials for SIBs, the poor conductivity and huge volume expansion limit its practical application. Meanwhile, Ge is also regarded as a promising anode material for SIBs. Its electrical conductivity and ion diffusivity are ∼100 times and 400 times those of Si, respectively. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref31'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref31" aria-label="reference 31">(31)</a> Thus, we hypothesized that a promising approach to enhance the conductivity of P could be via Ge alloying. Although it is an expensive material, we can affordably ameliorate the low-conductivity problem of P by using small amount of active metal components. In GeP<sub>5</sub> material, the content of Ge is little. Moreover, the GeP<sub>5</sub> has been proved to have excellent lithium storage properties. Li et al. reported that GeP<sub>5</sub>/C anode for LIBs delivered excellent rate performance and a high initial Coulombic efficiency. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref41'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref41" aria-label="reference 41">(41)</a> However, there are few works that were previously explored for GeP<sub>5</sub> as an anode material for SIBs. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref42 ref43'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref42 ref43" aria-label="reference 42 and 43">(42,43)</a> The AB shows the good electrical conductivity. With the particle size of about dozens of nanometers, it can contribute to mixing homogeneously with GeP<sub>5</sub> nanoparticles. Moreover, GO has large specific surface area where AB and GeP<sub>5</sub> nanoparticles uniformly disperse, mitigating volume expansion during the sodiation/desodiation. Therefore, a dual-carbon network of AB/GO is a good choice to enhance the electrochemical performance of GeP<sub>5</sub> as an anode material for SIBs.</div><div class="NLM_p last">In this work, the GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO composite is successfully prepared via a simple technique of ball milling. The ultrasmall GeP<sub>5</sub> and AB nanoparticles are uniformly dispersed on the layers of graphene oxide, forming the dual-carbon conductive network structure. The electrochemical tests corroborate that the GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO composite exhibits greatly improved sodium storage performance. Moreover, it has the best performance compared to that of the AB-modified GeP<sub>5</sub> (GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB) and GO-modified GeP<sub>5</sub> (GeP<sub>5</sub>/GO) composite. In detail, the GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO composite delivers a high reversible capacity of 597.5 and 175 mAh/g at the current density of 0.1 and 5.0 A/g, respectively. The excellent sodium storage performance is benefitted from the small particle size and the special dual-carbon conductive network structure. The former can shorten the transport path of the Na<sup>+</sup>. The latter can improve the conductivity of the electrode and effectively alleviate the volume expansion during discharge/charge process.</div></div><div id="sec2" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i3">2.  Experimental Section</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div id="sec2_1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i4" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i4">2.1.  Preparation of the GeP<sub>5</sub> and GeP<sub>5</sub> Composites</h3><div class="NLM_p last">All reagents were used without any treatment after purchase. Red phosphorus (P, Sigma-Aldrich) and Germanium powder (Ge, Sigma-Aldrich) were weighed according to the composition of GeP<sub>5</sub>. The total mass is ∼4 g. The elements were loaded into a stainless-steel ball milling jar in a glovebox under an argon atmosphere with an oxygen and water level below 0.1 ppm. The materials were ball-milled for 2 h by using the 8000D Mixer/Mill-dual high-energy ball mill. The GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO composite was synthesized in two steps. First, 10 mg of GO and 20 mg of AB nanoparticles were ball-milled for 12 h under the protection of an argon atmosphere. And then, 60 mg of pure GeP<sub>5</sub> was milled to the above mixture for 2 h. In addition, the GeP<sub>5</sub> was mixed with GO and AB nanoparticles using the same weight ratios to prepare the GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB and GeP<sub>5</sub>/GO composites, respectively, with the same process as that for the preparation for the GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO composite.</div></div><div id="sec2_2" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i5" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i5">2.2.  Material Characterization</h3><div class="NLM_p last">Powder X-ray diffraction (XRD) patterns were collected from the Rigaku D/Smartlab (Cu Ka radiation). The morphology of the prepared materials was characterized by transmission electron microscopy (TEM, JEOL-2100 F, 200 kV) and scanning electron microscopy (SEM) (HITACHI-SU8010, 10 kV). The element mappings were performed by using the energy dispersive X-ray spectroscopy.</div></div><div id="sec2_3" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i6" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i6">2.3.  Electrochemical Measurements</h3><div class="NLM_p last">Electrochemical performance was tested in 2032 coin cells. The GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO electrode was prepared by coating the slurry of the GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO (90 wt %) and CMC (10 wt %) onto the copper foil (no extra conductive additives). For comparison, the GeP<sub>5</sub>, GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB, and GeP<sub>5</sub>/GO electrodes were also consisted of 70 wt % pure GeP<sub>5</sub>, GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB, and GeP<sub>5</sub>/GO, respectively, and 20 wt % conductive additives (AB) and 10 wt % CMC. And then, the prepared electrode was dried at 60 °C in vacuum for one night. The mass loading of the electrode material is about 1.5 mg/cm<sup>3</sup>. The electrolyte was 1.0 mol/L NaClO<sub>4</sub> in a mixed solvent of ethylene carbonate and propylene carbonate in a 1:1 volume ratio with 5% fluoroethylene carbonate. The coin cell was assembled in the glovebox filled with argon and the oxygen and moisture content of below 0.1 ppm. The constant current charge/discharge measurements were performed on a LAND (Wuhan Kingnuo Electronics, China) cycler. The cyclic voltammetry (CV) curves were captured on the CHI 750 system (Chenhua Instruments, China).</div></div></div><div id="sec3" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i7">3.  Results and Discussion</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p">The GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO composite was prepared as an anode material for SIBs by ball milling. As shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>, the GeP<sub>5</sub> nanoparticles are surrounded by AB nanoparticles forming carbon conductive network. Then, they are uniformly dispersed on the layers of graphene oxide, forming the structure of the dual-carbon conductive network. The dual-carbon network will not only shorten the transport distance of the Na<sup>+</sup> and electron but also relax the huge volume change during the charge/discharge process, which greatly improves the rate and cycle performance of the electrode material. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref1 ref34'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref1 ref34" aria-label="reference 1 and 34">(1,34)</a></div><figure id="fig1" data-index="1" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 1</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11103/asset/images/medium/am-2018-111039_0001.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11103/asset/images/large/am-2018-111039_0001.jpeg" id="gr1" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 1. Illustration of the synthesis process for the GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO composite.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11103/asset/images/large/am-2018-111039_0001.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.8b11103&amp;id=fig1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p"><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>a shows the X-ray diffraction (XRD) patterns for the GeP<sub>5</sub> nanoparticles and GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO composite. The diffraction peaks of the high-energy mechanical milling prepared GeP<sub>5</sub> nanoparticles can be clearly detected. However, for GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO composite, the intensity of GeP<sub>5</sub> phase’s diffraction peaks is sharply decreased. This is caused by the decadence of the GeP<sub>5</sub> crystallization, the reduced particle size, and carbon coating, which can be proved by the scanning electron microscopy (SEM). <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref34 ref44'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref34 ref44" aria-label="reference 34 and 44">(34,44)</a> And as shown in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.8b11103/suppl_file/am8b11103_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S1</a>, the intensity ratio of D band and G band (<i>I</i><sub>D</sub>/<i>I</i><sub>G</sub>) of the GO, AB/p-rGO, and GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO is 0.91, 1.04, and 1.05, respectively. The result indicates that the GO is partially reduced to rGO during ball milling. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref45'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref45" aria-label="reference 45">(45)</a> As shown in the SEM images of GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO composite (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>b,c) and GeP<sub>5</sub> nanoparticles (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>d), the GeP<sub>5</sub> and AB nanoparticles are uniformly dispersed on the layers of GO. Moreover, the GeP<sub>5</sub> nanoparticles are surrounded by the AB nanoparticle-formed carbon conductive network, forming the structure of the dual-carbon conductive network. This dual-carbon conductive network provides more pathways of electron and will effectively alleviate the stress of volume expansion during sodiation/desodiation reactions. Furthermore, the size of the GeP<sub>5</sub> is greatly reduced from hundreds of nanometers to dozens of nanometers, which efficaciously shortens the path for Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion and mitigates the strain during the sodiation/desodiation process. This structure is also confirmed from the transmission electron microscope (TEM) tests. As shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>e,f, AB nanoparticles are distributed on the GO sheets with a particle size of about 50 nm. The high-resolution TEM (HRTEM) shows the lattice spacing of 0.257 nm, which corresponds to that of the (012) crystal planes of the GeP<sub>5</sub> (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.8b11103/suppl_file/am8b11103_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S2</a>). <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref34'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref34" aria-label="reference 34">(34)</a> Moreover, it is clearly shown that the GeP<sub>5</sub> nanoparticles with a diameter of about 10 nm are embedded in the AB conductive network. As shown in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.8b11103/suppl_file/am8b11103_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S3</a>, the elemental mapping of the GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO composite corroborates the homogeneous distribution of Ge (green), P (red), C (blue), and oxygen (red). This proves that the GeP<sub>5</sub>, AB, and GO are uniformly distributed in the GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO composite by the method of ball milling.</div><figure id="fig2" data-index="2" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 2</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11103/asset/images/medium/am-2018-111039_0002.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11103/asset/images/large/am-2018-111039_0002.jpeg" id="gr2" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 2. (a) XRD patterns of the GeP<sub>5</sub> nanoparticles and GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO composite, (b, c) the SEM images of the GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO composite. (d) SEM image of the GeP<sub>5</sub> nanoparticles. (e) TEM image of the GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO composite. (f) HRTEM image of the GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO composite.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11103/asset/images/large/am-2018-111039_0002.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.8b11103&amp;id=fig2"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">The electrochemical properties of the GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO composite are evaluated in half cells. <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>a shows the cyclic voltammetry curves (CVs) of the GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO composite electrode at a scan rate of 0.1 mV/s for the first five cycles. During the first discharge process, the irreversible cathodic peak at about 0.7 V can be assigned to the side reaction of the solid electrolyte interface (SEI) film formation. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref42'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref42" aria-label="reference 42">(42)</a> The big broad cathodic peak of 0.22 V could be vested in the Na<sup>+</sup> insertion reaction with the GeP<sub>5</sub> to form the NaGe and Na<sub>3</sub>P. In the subsequent cathodic scans, the peak of 0.22 V splits into two peaks of 0.22 and 0.84 V. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref42'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref42" aria-label="reference 42">(42)</a> And the anodic peaks of 0.51 and 1.56 V can correspond to a stepwise desodiation process from the Na<sub>3</sub>P phase to form intermediates of NaP, Na<sub>3</sub>P<sub>11</sub>, NaP<sub>7</sub>, and P, respectively, which indicates a multistep redox reaction. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref46 ref47 ref48'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref46 ref47 ref48" aria-label="reference 46 to 48">(46−48)</a> Furthermore, the broad peak at 0.76 V belongs to the desodiation process from the Na<sub>3</sub>P and NaGe phases. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref42'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref42" aria-label="reference 42">(42)</a> The other three materials show similar peaks in the first cycles (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.8b11103/suppl_file/am8b11103_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S4</a>). The well-overlapped curves in the following four cycles indicate superior sodiation/desodiation reversibility of the GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO composite electrode. This process can be attributed to the following <a class="ref internalNav" href="#eq1" aria-label="reactions 1">reactions </a><a class="ref internalNav" href="#eq1" aria-label="1">1</a>–<a class="ref internalNav" href="#eq3" aria-label="3">3</a>. It can be calculated that the theoretical capacity of GeP<sub>5</sub> is 1888 mAh/g. The Ge contributes 118 mAh/g, and the 5 P contribute 1770 mAh/g.<span class="NLM_disp-formula"><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq1"><div class="equation"><img class="imgWithoutFigViewer " src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11103/asset/images/medium/am-2018-111039_m001.gif" alt="" id="_i8"></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(1)</span></div></div></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula"><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq2"><div class="equation"><img class="imgWithoutFigViewer " src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11103/asset/images/medium/am-2018-111039_m002.gif" alt="" id="_i9"></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(2)</span></div></div></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula"><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq3"><div class="equation"><img class="imgWithoutFigViewer " src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11103/asset/images/medium/am-2018-111039_m003.gif" alt="" id="_i10"></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(3)</span></div></div></span>The discharge/charge curves of the GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO composite electrode are tested between the voltage of 0.01 and 2.8 V at the current of 0.1 A/g (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>b). The discharge plateau of the first cycle at about 0.7 V is the side reaction of the solid electrolyte interface (SEI) film formation, which is consistent with the peak at 0.7 V of CV. And the plateau of 0.22 V belongs to the Na<sup>+</sup> insertion reaction with the GeP<sub>5</sub> to form the NaGe and Na<sub>3</sub>P. The charge plateaus at 0.36, 0.51, and 0.76 V correspond to a stepwise desodiation process from the Na<sub>3</sub>P phase, consistent with the results of the CV. But the plateau of 1.56 V is unconspicuous. The well-overlapped curves suggest the good cycle stability for GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO composite as SIB anode.</div><figure id="fig3" data-index="3" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 3</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11103/asset/images/medium/am-2018-111039_0003.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11103/asset/images/large/am-2018-111039_0003.jpeg" id="gr3" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 3. Sodium storage mechanism of the GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO composite. (a) CV curves of the initial five cycles at the scan rate of 0.1 mV/s; (b) discharge/charge curves of the initial five cycles at the current density of 0.1 A/g.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11103/asset/images/large/am-2018-111039_0003.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.8b11103&amp;id=fig3"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p"><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">4</a>a shows the discharge and charge curves of the GeP<sub>5</sub> nanoparticles and the other three carbon-compounding composites (GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB, GeP<sub>5</sub>/GO and GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO) for the first several cycles. The test is carried out at the voltage of 0.01–2.8 V, at the current of 0.1 A/g. The discharge curve of the GeP<sub>5</sub> nanoparticles at the first cycle exhibits two flat voltage plateaus at 0.7–0.5 V and below 0.5 V, which belong to the formation of the SEI film and the Na<sup>+</sup> insertion to the GeP<sub>5</sub>, respectively. And the charge voltage plateau can vest in the desodiation from Na<sub>3</sub>P. But it is different from the other three carbon-compounding composites (GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB, GeP<sub>5</sub>/GO, and GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO) in that the voltage plateau is short at the second charge curve. It is difficult to achieve dealloying due to electrode pulverization during the sodiation/desodiation process. Also, the quick capacity decay can be ascribed to large volume expansion during cycling, besides the electrode pulverization and formation of thick SEI film. The main discharge voltage plateaus of carbon composites are similar to those of the pure GeP<sub>5</sub> nanoparticles. The plateaus at 0.51 and 1.56 V can be corresponded to a stepwise desodiation process from the Na<sub>3</sub>P phase to intermediates of NaP, Na<sub>3</sub>P<sub>11</sub>, NaP<sub>7</sub>, and P, respectively. Furthermore, the plateau at 0.76 V can belong to the desodiation process of Na<sub>3</sub>P and NaGe phase. After several cycles, the capacity of the GeP<sub>5</sub>, GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB, GeP<sub>5</sub>/GO, and GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO is successively 124, 330, 302, and 564 mAh/g with the capacity retention ratio of 27.7, 87.5, 26.0, and 94.5%, respectively. This suggests that dual-carbon composite has greatly enhanced the cycle performance than with pure GeP<sub>5</sub>. The rate performances of the four materials with current densities of 0.1, 0.2, 0.5, 1.0, 2.0, and 5.0 A/g are shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">4</a>b. The GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO composite not only exhibits the highest reversible capacity but also shows the best rate performance than that of the other three materials. The reversible capacities of the GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO composite are 575, 477, 374, 311, 243, and 163 mAh/g at the current density of 0.1, 0.2, 0.5, 1.0, 2.0, and 5.0 A/g, respectively (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.8b11103/suppl_file/am8b11103_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S5</a>). More remarkably, the GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO composite still retains a high capacity of 163 mAh/g at the large current density of 5.0 A/g. When the current density reverts to 0.1 A/g, the capacity of the GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO composite can return to 555 mAh/g, indicating the excellent rate performance that benefits from the dual-carbon conductive network structure. The cycle performances of the GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO composite, GeP<sub>5</sub>, GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB, and GeP<sub>5</sub>/GO electrode materials at the current of 0.5 A/g are shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">4</a>c. Obviously, the GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO composite shows the best cycle performance with the least capacity attenuation. All carbon-compounding composites exhibit higher capacity retention than that of the pristine GeP<sub>5</sub> nanoparticles. The reversible capacities of the GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO, GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB, and GeP<sub>5</sub>/GO composites are about 400, 200, and 50 mAh/g after 50 cycles. The capacity retention ratios are about 81.6, 66.7, and 5.9%, respectively. However, the reversible capacity of the pristine GeP<sub>5</sub> nanoparticles almost attenuates to zero after three cycles. The improved cycle performance of the carbon-compounding composite attributes to the carbon conductive network, which can not only relieve the stress of volume expansion but provide fast electron transmission paths during the sodiation/desodiation process. Thus, the GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO composite shows the best sodium storage performance with the benefits of the special dual-carbon conductive network structure. The results demonstrated that the carbon conductive network of the GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO composite formed by the AB nanoparticles and GO network not only provides more paths of electron and Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion but also is a good buffer of volume expansion of the materials, which results in the superior cycle performance of the GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO composite.</div><figure id="fig4" data-index="4" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 4</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11103/asset/images/medium/am-2018-111039_0004.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11103/asset/images/large/am-2018-111039_0004.jpeg" id="gr4" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 4. (a) Galvanostatic curves of the initial five cycles of the GeP<sub>5</sub>/GO, GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO, and GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB and two cycles of GeP<sub>5</sub> at the current density of 0.1 A/g. The comparison of (b) rate capabilities and (c) long cycling stability among GeP<sub>5</sub>, GeP<sub>5</sub>/GO, GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO, and GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11103/asset/images/large/am-2018-111039_0004.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.8b11103&amp;id=fig4"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">To further study the sodium storage mechanism of the GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO composite, as shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">5</a>a, the CV curves have been tested to investigate the kinetic process at different scan rates of 0.1, 0.2, 0.3, 0.5, and 1 mV/s. The result reveals that the peak current of the material is not proportional to the square root of the scan rate, which indicates that both nonfaradaic and faradaic processes are contained <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref49'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref49" aria-label="reference 49">(49)</a><span class="NLM_disp-formula"><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq4"><div class="equation"><img class="imgWithoutFigViewer " src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11103/asset/images/medium/am-2018-111039_m004.gif" alt="" id="_i11"></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(4)</span></div></div></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula"><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq5"><div class="equation"><img class="imgWithoutFigViewer " src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11103/asset/images/medium/am-2018-111039_m005.gif" alt="" id="_i12"></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(5)</span></div></div></span>where <i>a</i> and <i>b</i> are adjustable parameters. For <i>b</i> = 0.5, the sodium storage procedure of the GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO composite is mainly controlled by the diffusion behaviors. For <i>b</i> ∼ 1, the sodium storage procedure of the GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO composite is the main subject to the pseudocapacitive behaviors. log(<i>i</i>) vs log(<i>v</i>) plots of the sample at three redox peaks are present in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">5</a>b.The slope of the plot is <i>b</i>-value. The results reveal that the <i>b</i>-values of the GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO composite are 0.79, 0.64, and 0.79 at peaks 1, 2, and 3, respectively. Values approaching 1 suggest that the charge/discharge process of the GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO composite is related to both diffusion reaction and capacitive behavior. Furthermore, the capacitive contribution at various scan rates is calculated by the following equation (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">5</a>c)<span class="NLM_disp-formula"><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq6"><div class="equation"><img class="imgWithoutFigViewer " src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11103/asset/images/medium/am-2018-111039_m006.gif" alt="" id="_i13"></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(6)</span></div></div></span>where <i>k</i><sub>1</sub><i>v</i> and <i>k</i><sub>2</sub><i>v</i><sup>0.5</sup> represent the capacitive and the diffusion contributions, respectively. As shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">5</a>d, the capacitive contributions of the GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO composite are 55.6, 65.2, 68.7, 73.5, and 79.6% at different scan rates of 0.1, 0.2, 0.3, 0.5, and 1 mV/s, respectively. The results further indicate that the sodium storage procedure of the GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO composite is mainly controlled by the pseudocapacitive behaviors. This is the reason for GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO composite shows fast reaction kinetics and best rate performance compared to those of GeP<sub>5</sub>, GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB, and GeP<sub>5</sub>/GO. The EIS measurements are conducted to further investigate the electrochemical performance of GeP<sub>5</sub> via the dual-carbon conductive network modification. <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.8b11103/suppl_file/am8b11103_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S7</a> shows the comparison of the typical Nyquist plots (<i>Z</i><sub>re</sub> vs −<i>Z</i><sub>im</sub>) between GeP<sub>5</sub> and the other three GeP<sub>5</sub>/carbon composites in half cells before cycling. It is disclosed clearly that three GeP<sub>5</sub>/carbon composites show smaller impedance (the smaller diameter of the semicircle in Nyquist plots) than that of GeP<sub>5</sub> anode, demonstrating that the strategy of carbon-compounding can significantly improve their electrical conductivity. Moreover, the GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO composite has the smallest impedance among the three composites, which is consistent with the above Na<sup>+</sup> storage performance.</div><figure id="fig5" data-index="5" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 5</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11103/asset/images/medium/am-2018-111039_0005.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11103/asset/images/large/am-2018-111039_0005.jpeg" id="gr5" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 5. (a) CV curves of the GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO at different scan rates from 0.1 to 1.0 mV/s, (b) log(<i>i</i>) vs log(<i>v</i>) plots for the GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO, (c) CV curve with the pseudocapacitive fraction shown by the dark cyan region of the GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO at a scan rate of 1 mV/s, (d) the pseudocapacitive contribution of the GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO at different scan rates.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11103/asset/images/large/am-2018-111039_0005.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.8b11103&amp;id=fig5"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">As shown in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.8b11103/suppl_file/am8b11103_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S7</a>, the initial Coulombic efficiency of the GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO composite is about 60% and the next cycle is 95%, close to 100%, showing the best cycle performance than that of the other three materials. Furthermore, the superior electrochemical performance of the GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO composite compared to that of GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB and GeP<sub>5</sub>/GO composite is benefitted from the special structure of dual-carbon conductive network, as shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">6</a>. The dual-carbon conductive network provides more transport pathways for the electron, and the small particle size can shorten the transport path of the Na<sup>+</sup>, both of which improve the electrochemical reaction kinetics and contribute to better electrochemical performance of the GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO composite as an anode for SIBs. Furthermore, the flexible dual-carbon conductive network can not only improve the conductivity of the electrode but also effectively alleviate the volume expansion of the electrodes during discharging/charging process, improving the cycle performance of the anode material.</div><figure id="fig6" data-index="6" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 6</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11103/asset/images/medium/am-2018-111039_0006.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11103/asset/images/large/am-2018-111039_0006.jpeg" id="gr6" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 6. Illustration of the rational design for the (a) GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO, (b) GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB, and (c) GeP<sub>5</sub>/GO anode.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11103/asset/images/large/am-2018-111039_0006.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.8b11103&amp;id=fig6"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">To further testify the superior cycle performance of the GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO composite, the SEM images of the GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO composite anode before and after cycling are shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">7</a>. <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">7</a>a is the SEM image of the pristine GeP<sub>5</sub> anode before cycling, and <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">7</a>b,c shows the morphology of the GeP<sub>5</sub> anode after 10 cycles. It is clearly shown that the pristine GeP<sub>5</sub> anode has cracked and pulverized after 10 cycles. On the contrary, as shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">7</a>d,e, the integrity of GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO anode is very well retained after 30 cycles. As shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">7</a>f, the special dual-carbon structure remains intact, powerfully proving that the structure of the prepared GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO composite is very stable. And it is expected to be used as an anode material for sodium-ion batteries. And <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.8b11103/suppl_file/am8b11103_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Table S1</a> shows the comparison of the cycle performance between the GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO and previous works. So far, only two works have reported GeP<sub>5</sub> anode for SIBs. The GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO composite exhibits good cycle performance at larger current density of 0.5 A/g. Moreover, this work provides a novel design of a dual-carbon conductive network to improve the electrochemical performance of GeP<sub>5</sub> anode for the first time.</div><figure id="fig7" data-index="7" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 7</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11103/asset/images/medium/am-2018-111039_0007.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11103/asset/images/large/am-2018-111039_0007.jpeg" id="gr7" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 7. Morphologic changes of the surface on the electrodes upon cell test: (a) the fresh electrode and (b, c) the electrode after 10 cycles of the GeP<sub>5</sub> anode; (d) the fresh electrode and (e, f) the electrode after 30 cycles of the GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO anode.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b11103/asset/images/large/am-2018-111039_0007.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.8b11103&amp;id=fig7"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure></div><div id="sec4" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i14">4.  Conclusions</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p last">The GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO composite with dual-carbon conductive network is successfully prepared as an anode material for SIBs by a simple technique of ball milling. The dual-carbon conductive network structure is formed by GeP<sub>5</sub> and AB nanoparticles uniformly dispersed on the GO layers. The GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO composite exhibits significantly improved Na-storage properties compared to those of GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB and GeP<sub>5</sub>/GO composites. As the anode material for SIBs, it exhibits excellent rate performance and delivers a large reversible capacity of 175 mAh/g at the current density of 5.0 A/g. Remarkably, the GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO composite shows the reversible capacity of 400 mAh/g after 50 cycles at the current density of 0.5 A/g. This excellent rate and cycle performance benefit from the small size of the GeP<sub>5</sub> and the special dual-carbon conductive network structure. The former shortens the Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion paths, and the latter provides more transport paths of electron.</div></div><div class="NLM_back"><div class="article_supporting-info" id="notes-1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i15">Supporting Information</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><p class="last">The Supporting Information is available free of charge on the <a href="/" class="ext-link">ACS Publications website</a> at DOI: <a href="/doi/abs/10.1021/acsami.8b11103" class="ext-link">10.1021/acsami.8b11103</a>.</p><ul class="NLM_list-list_type-label" id="silist"><li><p class="inline">Raman spectra of the GO, AB/p-rGO, and GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO composite; HRTEM image of the GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO composite; SEM image and elemental mapping of the GeP<sub>5</sub>/AB/p-rGO composite; comparison of CV curves, EIS spectra, and the Coulombic efficiency (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.8b11103/suppl_file/am8b11103_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">PDF</a>)</p></li></ul><p></p><div class="supInfoBoxOnFTP "><div class="sup-info-attachments"><ul><li><a class="suppl-anchor" href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.8b11103/suppl_file/am8b11103_si_001.pdf">am8b11103_si_001.pdf (1.37 MB)</a></li></ul></div></div></div><div class="testing" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.8b11103" data-url="https://widgets.figshare.com/static/figshare.js" id="figshare-widget" style="display: block;"></div><div class="TermsAndConditionsDropzone3" data-pb-dropzone="TermsAndConditionsDropzone3"><div data-widget-def="UX3HTMLWidget" data-widget-id="85b54935-30e9-4058-a6d2-0b40fb754a85" class="mb-4">

                        cas_cit3R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">3</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Room-temperature stationary sodium-ion batteries for large-scale electric energy storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Pan, Huilin; Hu, Yong-Sheng; Chen, Liquan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Room-temp. stationary sodium-ion batteries have attracted great attention particularly in large-scale elec. energy storage applications for renewable energy and smart grid because of the huge abundant sodium resources and low cost.  In this article, a variety of electrode materials including cathodes and anodes as well as electrolytes for room-temp. stationary sodium-ion batteries are briefly reviewed.  We compare the difference in storage behavior between Na and Li in their analogous electrodes and summarize the sodium storage mechanisms in the available electrode materials.  This review also includes some new results from our group and our thoughts on developing new materials.  Some perspectives and directions on designing better materials for practical applications are pointed out based on knowledge from the literature and our experience.  Through this extensive literature review, the search for suitable electrode and electrolyte materials for stationary sodium-ion batteries is still challenging.  However, after intensive research efforts, we believe that low-cost, long-life and room-temp. sodium-ion batteries would be promising for applications in large-scale energy storage system in the near future.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpqNKJTie6WmbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liXSLTPNVe9sQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhtFOisrzJ&amp;md5=2e02460553edc21e1ea8b73982ed63bb</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref4'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit4" data-doi="10.1039/c3ee41031e"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Palomares, V.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Casas-Cabanas, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Castillo-Martinez, E.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, M.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review is given.  Li metal battery, one of the most promising candidates for high-energy-d. storage system, has attracted extensive interest due to its extremely high theor. specific capacity, low gravimetric d. and lowest neg. redox potential.  However, the formation of lithium dendrites, uncontrolled interfacial reactions, and huge vol. change during the cycles of charging and discharging lower the Coulombic efficiency and cause harsh safety issues; they are the major hurdles towards the practical applications of lithium metal batteries.  This paper presents the recent advances in Li metal battery and focuses on the functional hybrid electrodes, which are constructed to boost the electrochem. performance of metallic Li and suppress the growth of Li dendrites.  Their general design rules, fabrication strategies, enhanced performances, and potential applications are summarized and analyzed.                         cas_cit6R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">6</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Two-dimensional vermiculite separator for lithium sulfur batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xu, Rui; Sun, Yingzhi; Wang, Yunfei; Huang, Jiaqi; Zhang, Qiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chinese Chemical Letters</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Lithium-sulfur batteries have been considered as one of the most promising battery system for their high theor. energy d.  However, the lithium-sulfur batteries suffer from the dissoln. and diffusion of polysulfides, which induce parasitic reactions with lithium metal anodes.  The safety of lithium-sulfur batteries is also concerned with the risk of dendrite growth on lithium metal anodes.  To simultaneously address the challenges in the shuttle effect and safety problems, we demonstrate herein a two-dimensional vermiculite separator.  With the assembly of the 2D exfoliated vermiculite sheets, the vermiculite separator can suppress the diffusion of polysulfides across the separator through electrostatic interaction and steric hindrance.  Meanwhile, the inorg. sheets with high strength and Young's modulus prevent the penetration of lithium metal dendrite and potentially improve the safety of the system.  This work elucidates a promising strategy for safe and stable lithium sulfur batteries, and can also be extended to other electrochem. systems based on metal anodes.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq7Siy5VitpLrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lglyoCoRBSySg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhs1yjsL%252FN&amp;md5=2d28924bcca648bd3b7d2123982ff387</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref7"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref7'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">7</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit7" data-doi="10.1002/advs.201600500"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiong, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hao, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Coordination of Surface-Induced Reaction and Intercalation: Toward a High-Performance Carbon Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.     </div><div class="casAbstract">Oxygen-rich carbon material is successfully fabricated from a porous carbon and evaluated as anode for sodium-ion battery.                         cas_cit8R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">8</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Tin and graphite based nanocomposites: Potential anode for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Datta, Moni Kanchan; Epur, Rigved; Saha, Partha; Kadakia, Karan; Park, Sung Kyoo; Kumta, Prashant N.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">225</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Pure Sn and a homogeneous nanocomposite of Sn and graphite (C), denoted as Sn/C, have been studied as a suitable anode for Na ion batteries.  The Sn/C nanocomposites have been synthesized by high energy mech. milling (HEMM) of pure Sn and graphite of nominal compn. C-70% Sn.  Pure microcryst. Sn (≤44 μm) exhibits a 1st discharge capacity ∼856 mA-h g-1 which is close to the expected theor. capacity, however, it shows a large 1st cycle irreversible loss (∼67%) and the anticipated inevitable rapid fade in capacity expectedly due to structural failure of the electrode.  However, the resultant Sn/C based nanocomposite, synthesized by HEMM after 1h of milling, exhibits a 1st cycle discharge capacity ∼584 mA-h g-1 with a 1st cycle irreversible loss ∼30%.  The Sn/C nanocomposite shows a 1st cycle charge capacity of ∼410 mA-h g-1 with improved capacity retention in comparison to pure Sn displaying 0.7% fade in capacity per cycle up to 20 cycles when cycled at a rate of approx. C/8.  SEM anal. indicates that the structural integrity and microstructural stability of the Sn/C nanocomposite during the alloying/dealloying processes appear to be the primary factors contributing to the good cyclability obsd. in the above HEMM derived nanocomposite suggesting its promise as a potential anode for Na-ion systems.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrQLHelWVsLyrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lglyoCoRBSySg"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit9R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">9</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Black Phosphorus as a High-Capacity, High-Capability Negative Electrode for Sodium-Ion Batteries: Investigation of the Electrode/Electrolyte Interface</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Dahbi, Mouad; Yabuuchi, Naoaki; Fukunishi, Mika; Kubota, Kei; Chihara, Kuniko; Tokiwa, Kazuyasu; Yu, Xue-fang; Ushiyama, Hiroshi; Yamashita, Koichi; Son, Jin-Young; Cui, Yi-Tao; Oji, Hiroshi; Komaba, Shinichi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">For a nonaq. sodium-ion battery (NIB), phosphorus materials have been studied as the highest-capacity neg. electrodes.  However, the large vol. change of phosphorus upon cycling at low voltage causes the formation of new active surfaces and potentially results in electrolyte decompn. at the active surface, which remains one of the major limiting factors for the long cycling life of batteries.  In this present study, powerful surface characterization techniques are combined for investigation on the electrode/electrolyte interface of the black phosphorus electrodes with polyacrylate binder to understand the formation of a solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) in alkyl carbonate ester and its evolution during cycling.  The hard XPS (HAXPES) anal. suggests that SEI (passive film) consists of mainly inorg. species, which originate from decompn. of electrolyte solvents and additives.  The thicker surface layer is formed during cycling in the additive-free electrolyte, compared to that in the electrolyte with fluoroethylene carbonate (FEC) or vinylene carbonate (VC) additive.  The HAXPES and time-of-flight secondary ion mass spectroscopy (TOF-SIMS) studies further reveal accumulation of org. carbonate species near the surface and inorg. salt decompn. species.  These findings open paths for further improvement for the cyclability of phosphorus electrodes for high-energy NIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqcMIRYfr0XhbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljTQ6D3HoszRQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XisVygtbY%253D&amp;md5=fb5dc52d329e6ff1a088951643342c16</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref10"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref10'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">10</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit10"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, J.                         cas_cit12R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">12</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Cobalt Sulfide Quantum Dot Embedded N/S-Doped Carbon Nanosheets with Superior Reversibility and Rate Capability for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Guo, Qiubo; Ma, Yifan; Chen, Tingting; Xia, Qiuying; Yang, Mei; Xia, Hui; Yu, Yan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">11</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Metal sulfides are promising anode materials for sodium-ion batteries due to their large specific capacities.  The practical applications of metal sulfides in sodium-ion batteries, however, are still limited due to their large vol. expansion, poor cycling stability, and sluggish electrode kinetics.  In this work, a two-dimensional heterostructure of CoSx (CoS and Co9S8) quantum dots embedded N/S-doped carbon nanosheets (CoSx@NSC) is prepd. by a sol-gel method.  The CoSx quantum dots are in situ formed within ultrafine carbon nanosheets without further sulfidation, thus resulting in ultrafine CoSx particle size and embedded heterostructure.  Meanwhile, enriched N and S codoping in the carbon nanosheets greatly enhances the elec. cond. for the conductive matrix and creates more active sites for sodium storage.  As a result, the hybrid CoSx@NSC electrode shows excellent rate capability (600 mAh g-1 at 0.2 A g-1 and 500 mAh g-1 at 10 A g-1) and outstanding cycling stability (87% capacity retention after 200 cycles at 1 A g-1), making it promising as an anode material for high-performance sodium-ion batteries.  A CoSx@NSC//Na0.44MnO2 full cell is demonstrated, and it can deliver a specific capacity of 414 mAh g-1 (based on the mass of CoSx@NSC) at a c.d. of 0.2 A g-1.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq9OkEmDbmxnrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljTQ6D3HoszRQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhvVaku7bJ&amp;md5=366aa605bfae1bf5095b737a7b5b3c40</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref13"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref13'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">13</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit13" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2016.03.060"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lee, K.                         cas_cit13R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">13</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Long-term cycling stability of porous Sn anode for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim, Changhyeon; Lee, Ki-Young; Kim, Icpyo; Park, Jinsoo; Cho, Gyubong; Kim, Ki-Won; Ahn, Jou-Hyeon; Ahn, Hyo-Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A phase-inversion technique is introduced to produce a porous Sn anode for sodium batteries, which can accommodate vol. changes during sodiation and desodiation.                         cas_cit14R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">14</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A controlled red phosphorus@Ni-P core@shell nanostructure as an ultralong cycle-life and superior high-rate anode for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Shuai; Feng, Jinkui; Bian, Xiufang; Liu, Jie; Xu, Hui; An, Yongling</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">5</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1222-1233</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EESNBY</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1754-5706</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), a potential alternative to lithium ion batteries (LIBs), have attracted remarkable attention recently due to the natural abundance and low-cost of sodium.  Here, we have presented a comprehensive study on combining electroless deposition with chem. dealloying to control the shell thickness and compn. of a red phosphorus (RP)@Ni-P core@shell nanostructure as a high performance anode for SIBs.  For the first time depending on regulating the dealloying time (1 h, 4 h, 8 h, 10 h and 20 h) of RP@Ni-P synthesized by electroless deposition of Ni on RP, 1 h RP@Ni-P, 4 h RP@Ni-P, 8 h RP@Ni-P, 10 h RP@Ni-P and 20 h RP@Ni-P with different shell thicknesses and compns. were prepd.  The in situ generated Ni2P on RP particle surfaces can facilitate intimate contact between RP and a mech. strong amorphous Ni-P outer shell with a high electronic cond., which ensures strong electrode structural integrity, a stable solid electrolyte interphase and ultra-fast electronic transport.  As a result, the 8 h RP@Ni-P composite presents a super high capacity (1256.2 mA h gcomposite-1 after 200 cycles at 260 mA gcomposite-1), superior rate capability (491 mA h gcomposite-1 at 5200 mA gcomposite-1) and unprecedented ultralong cycle-life at 5000 mA gcomposite-1 for an RP-based SIB anode (409.1 mA h gcomposite-1 after 2000 cycles).  This simple scalable synthesis approach will provide a new strategy for the optimization of core@shell nanostructures, paving the way for mass prodn. of high performance electrodes for SIBs and other energy storage systems.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoVRwOrxeWHubVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljTQ6D3HoszRQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXlsVyqurg%253D&amp;md5=5a9d70a9ec338f9b2bf0d110723db337</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref15"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref15'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">15</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit15"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yao, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xing-long, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xie, H.-m.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, l.-q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, R.-s.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">New Development of Lithium-Sulfur Batteries</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit17R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">17</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High Capacity of Hard Carbon Anode in Na-Ion Batteries Unlocked by POx Doping</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Zhifei; Ma, Lu; Surta, Todd Wesley; Bommier, Clement; Jian, Zelang; Xing, Zhenyu; Stickle, William F.; Dolgos, Michelle; Amine, Khalil; Lu, Jun; Wu, Tianpin; Ji, Xiulei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Energy Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">1</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">395-401</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AELCCP</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2380-8195</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The capacity of hard carbon anodes in Na-ion batteries rarely reaches values beyond 300 mAh/g.  It is reported that doping POx into local structures of hard carbon increases its reversible capacity from 283-359 mAh/g.  It is confirmed that the doped POx is redox inactive by X-ray adsorption near edge structure measurements, thus not contributing to the higher capacity.  Two significant changes are obsd. of hard carbon's local structures caused by doping.  First, the (002) d-spacing inside the turbostratic nanodomains is increased, revealed by both lab. and synchrotron X-ray diffraction.  Second, doping turns turbostratic nanodomains more defective along ab planes, indicated by neutron total scattering and the assocd. pair distribution function studies.  The local structural changes of hard carbon are correlated to the higher capacity, where both the plateau and slope regions in the potential profiles are enhanced.  The study demonstrates that Na-ion storage in hard carbon heavily depends on carbon local structures, where such structures, despite being disordered, can be tuned toward unusually high capacities.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqdu855Pkblf7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lguT_IKvPCy1g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhtFOktLvL&amp;md5=1451c96d6ecdb7b2271ab49cd240507b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref18'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit18" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201403734"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jache, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Adelhelm, P.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Use of Graphite as a Highly Reversible Electrode with Superior Cycle Life for Sodium-Ion Batteries by Making Use of Co-Intercalation Phenomena</span>. <i>Angew.
