                10.1002/anie.201403734</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D53%26publication_year%3D2014%26pages%3D10169-10173%26journal%3DAngew.%2BChem.%252C%2BInt.%2BEd.%26author%3DB.%2BJache%26author%3DP.%2BAdelhelm%26title%3DUse%2Bof%2BGraphite%2Bas%2Ba%2BHighly%2BReversible%2BElectrode%2Bwith%2BSuperior%2BCycle%2BLife%2Bfor%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%2Bby%2BMaking%2BUse%2Bof%2BCo-Intercalation%2BPhenomena%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fanie.201403734&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.8b11103&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fanie.201403734&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit18R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">18</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Use of Graphite as a Highly Reversible Electrode with Superior Cycle Life for Sodium-Ion Batteries by Making Use of Co-Intercalation Phenomena</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jache, Birte; Adelhelm, Philipp</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">53</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">38</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">10169-10173</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ACIEF5</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1433-7851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Although being the std. anode material in Li-ion batteries (LIBs), graphite so far is considered to fail application in Na-ion batteries (NIBs) because the Na-C system lacks suitable binary intercalation compds.  This limitation can be circumvented by using co-intercalation phenomena in a diglyme-based electrolyte.  The resulting compd. is a stage-I ternary intercalation compd. with an estd. stoichiometry of Na(diglyme)2C20.  Highlights of the electrode reaction are its high energy efficiency, the small irreversible loss during the 1st cycle, and a superior cycle life with capacities close to 100 mA-h g-1 for 1000 cycles and coulomb efficiencies &gt;99.87%.  A 1-to-one comparison with the analog Li-based cell shows that the Na-based system performs better and also withstands higher currents.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrIP5gn46fMJLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lguT_IKvPCy1g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXht1WlsbbE&amp;md5=80e4b709236b714939a54f259d959661</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref19"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref19'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">19</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit19" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201402984"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hong, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Park, Y.-U.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hwang, I.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kang, K.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sodium Storage Behavior in Natural Graphite using Ether-based Electrolyte Systems</span>. <i>Adv. Funct. Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>25</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">534</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">541</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/adfm.201402984</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D25%26publication_year%3D2015%26pages%3D534-541%26journal%3DAdv.%2BFunct.%2BMater.%26author%3DH.%2BKim%26author%3DJ.%2BHong%26author%3DY.-U.%2BPark%26author%3DJ.%2BKim%26author%3DI.%2BHwang%26author%3DK.%2BKang%26title%3DSodium%2BStorage%2BBehavior%2Bin%2BNatural%2BGraphite%2Busing%2BEther-based%2BElectrolyte%2BSystems%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fadfm.201402984&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.8b11103&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fadfm.201402984&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit19R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">19</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sodium Storage Behavior in Natural Graphite using Ether-based Electrolyte Systems</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim, Haegyeom; Hong, Jihyun; Park, Young-Uk; Kim, Jinsoo; Hwang, Insang; Kang, Kisuk</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">25</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">534-541</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AFMDC6</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1616-301X</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">This work reports that natural graphite is capable of Na insertion and extn. with a remarkable reversibility using ether-based electrolytes.  Natural graphite (the most well-known anode material for Li-ion batteries) has been barely studied as a suitable anode for Na rechargeable batteries due to the lack of Na intercalation capability.  Herein, graphite is not only capable of Na intercalation but also exhibits outstanding performance as an anode for Na-ion batteries.  The graphite anode delivers a reversible capacity of ≈150 mA-h/g with a cycle stability for 2500 cycles, and more than 75 mA-h/g at 10 A/g despite its micrometer-size (≈100 μm).  An Na storage mechanism in graphite, where Na+-solvent co-intercalation occurs combined with partial pseudocapacitive behaviors, is shown.  It is demonstrated that the electrolyte solvent species significantly affect the electrochem. properties, not only rate capability but also redox potential.  The feasibility of graphite in a Na full cell is also confirmed in conjunction with the Na1.5VPO4.8F0.7 cathode, delivering an energy of ≈120 W-h/kg while maintaining ≈70% of the initial capacity after 250 cycles.  This exceptional behavior of natural graphite promises new avenues for the development of cost-effective and reliable Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpH2c5ZOoUcVbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lguT_IKvPCy1g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhvFGiurrN&amp;md5=0bb4c36145b59a3b9727155eca307655</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref20"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref20'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">20</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit20" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201606023"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Noonan, O.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, C.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Tailored Yolk–Shell Sn@C Nanoboxes for High-Performance Lithium Storage</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Two-Dimensional SnO Anodes with a Tunable Number of Atomic Layers for Sodium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Fan; Zhu, Jiajie; Zhang, Daliang; Schwingenschlogl, Udo; Alshareef, Husam N.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">17</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1302-1311</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NALEFD</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1530-6984</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">We have systematically changed the no. of at. layers stacked in 2D SnO nanosheet anodes and studied their sodium ion battery (SIB) performance.  The results indicate that as the no. of at. SnO layers in a sheet decreases, both the capacity and cycling stability of the Na ion battery improve.  The thinnest SnO nanosheet anodes (two to six SnO monolayers) exhibited the best performance.  Specifically, an initial discharge and charge capacity of 1072 and 848 mAh g-1 were obsd., resp., at 0.1 A g-1.  In addn., an impressive reversible capacity of 665 mAh g-1 after 100 cycles at 0.1 A g-1 and 452 mAh g-1 after 1000 cycles at a high c.d. of 1.0 A g-1 was obsd., with excellent rate performance.  As the av. no. of at. layers in the anode sheets increased, the battery performance degraded significantly.  For example, for the anode sheets with 10-20 at. layers, only a reversible capacity of 389 mAh g-1 could be obtained after 100 cycles at 0.1 A g-1.  D. functional theory calcns. coupled with exptl. results were used to elucidate the sodiation mechanism of the SnO nanosheets.  This systematic study of monolayer-dependent phys. and electrochem. properties of 2D anodes shows a promising pathway to engineering and mitigating vol. changes in 2D anode materials for sodium ion batteries.  It also demonstrates that ultrathin SnO nanosheets are promising SIB anode materials with high specific capacity, stable cyclability, and excellent rate performance.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGok9B2_90thmbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lguT_IKvPCy1g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhs1ags7s%253D&amp;md5=fe1ee09c0528efe249c2ef4f38511755</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref22'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit22" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201603286"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, L.                 10.1021/acs.nanolett.7b01152</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D17%26publication_year%3D2017%26pages%3D3830-3836%26journal%3DNano%2BLett.%26author%3DM.%2BMao%26author%3DF.%2BYan%26author%3DC.%2BCui%26author%3DJ.%2BMa%26author%3DM.%2BZhang%26author%3DT.%2BWang%26author%3DC.%2BWang%26title%3DPipe-Wire%2BTiO2-Sn%2540Carbon%2BNanofibers%2BPaper%2BAnodes%2Bfor%2BLithium%2Band%2BSodium%2BIon%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facs.nanolett.7b01152&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.8b11103&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.7b01152&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit23R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">23</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Pipe-Wire TiO2-Sn@Carbon Nanofibers Paper Anodes for Lithium and Sodium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Mao, Minglei; Yan, Feilong; Cui, Chunyu; Ma, Jianmin; Zhang, Ming; Wang, Taihong; Wang, Chunsheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">17</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3830-3836</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NALEFD</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1530-6984</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Metallic tin has been considered as one of the most promising anode materials both for lithium (LIBs) and sodium ion battery (NIBs) because of a high theor. capacity and an appropriate low discharge potential.  However, Sn anodes suffer from a rapid capacity fading during cycling due to pulverization induced by severe vol. changes.  Here we innovatively synthesized pipe-wire TiO2-Sn@carbon nanofibers (TiO2-Sn@CNFs) via electrospinning and at. layer deposition to suppress pulverization-induced capacity decay.  In pipe-wire TiO2-Sn@CNFs paper, nano-Sn is uniformly dispersed in carbon nanofibers, which not only act as a buffer material to prevent pulverization, but also serve as a conductive matrix.  In addn., TiO2 pipe as the protection shell outside of Sn@carbon nanofibers can restrain the vol. variation to prevent Sn from aggregation and pulverization during cycling, thus increasing the Coulombic efficiency.  The pipe-wire TiO2-Sn@CNFs show excellent electrochem. performance as anodes for both LIBs and NIBs.  It exhibits a high and stable capacity of 643 mA h/g at 200 mA/g after 1100 cycles in LIBs and 413 mA h/g at 100 mA/g after 400 cycles in NIBs.  These results would shed light on the practical application of Sn-based materials as a high capacity electrode with good cycling stability for next-generation LIBs and NIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpWUZ-QZ7fVm7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhf885ZkxUsNQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXntFejs7w%253D&amp;md5=fa57f9269273896b449ad581fcc03917</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref24'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit24" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201505918"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bai, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qian, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Double-Walled Sb@TiO2–x Nanotubes as a Superior High-Rate and Ultralong-Lifespan Anode Material for Na-Ion and Li-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv. Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>28</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">4126</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">4133</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/adma.201505918</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D28%26publication_year%3D2016%26pages%3D4126-4133%26journal%3DAdv.%2BMater.%26author%3DN.%2BWang%26author%3DZ.%2BBai%26author%3DY.%2BQian%26author%3DJ.%2BYang%26title%3DDouble-Walled%2BSb%2540TiO2%25E2%2580%2593x%2BNanotubes%2Bas%2Ba%2BSuperior%2BHigh-Rate%2Band%2BUltralong-Lifespan%2BAnode%2BMaterial%2Bfor%2BNa-Ion%2Band%2BLi-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fadma.201505918&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.8b11103&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fadma.201505918&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Double-Walled Sb@TiO2-x Nanotubes as a Superior High-Rate and Ultralong-Lifespan Anode Material for Na-Ion and Li-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Nana; Bai, Zhongchao; Qian, Yitai; Yang, Jian</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">28</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">21</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4126-4133</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADVMEW</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0935-9648</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Here, double-walled cryst. Sb@amorphous TiO2-x nanotubes are synthesized by the calcination of Sb2S3@TiO2 nanorods in Ar/H2 produced by the hydrolysis of tetra-Bu titanate (TBOT) on Sb2S3 nanorods.  The formation of the double-walled structures could be assigned to the facile redn. of Sb2S3 and the strong interaction of Sb to TiO2.  Such a structure accommodates the vol. variation upon cycling well, then keeps the structure stable.  Meanwhile, this calcination in Ar/H2 also generates a lot of oxygen vacancies in the shell, supported by Ti3+ species in XPS spectra.  They would enhance the charge-transfer kinetics, particularly at the interface.  Thus, the double-walled nanotubes show excellent electrochem. performance as an anode material in the lithium-ion batteries and in sodium-ion batteries, both of which are on the top of the reported list.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrrrdrYefF6qrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhf885ZkxUsNQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XjtlKms7Y%253D&amp;md5=0bb077f676824aae644f1f5f12368294</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref25"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref25'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">25</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit25" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2016.06.018"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liao, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cui, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.                         cas_cit25R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">25</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Three dimensional self-assembly ZnSb nanowire balls with good performance as sodium ions battery anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liao, S.; Sun, Y.; Wang, Jing; Cui, H.; Wang, Chengxin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">211</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Novel 3D ZnSb nanowire balls composed of ultra-thin nanowires were achieved through simple self-assembly method based on typical thermodn. in chem. vapor deposition (CVD) system.  The elliptic cylinder-shaped nanowires with cross-section size of ∼25nm × ∼ 10 nm display impressive performance in sodium-ion battery (SIB) application as anode material.  Comparing to pure Sb, ZnSb is advantageous in resisting huge vol. change and possess enhanced cond., which would do much better to offer a long-time cycling stability and rate performance.  Such a small size of the low dimensional structures can further improve the electron/ion transfer efficiency.  Through systematic measurements, we found that, at 20 mA/g, the capacity remains 377mAh/g after the 100th cycle with the coulombic efficiency at ∼99%.  Even if the c.d. increased to 750 mA/g, the value was still higher than 225mAh/g.  The half-cell device also provides a rapid response and stable output in the rate tests (20-650 mA/g).  The good performance originates from the unique structural configuration, implying the huge potential value of ZnSb in SIB application.  We hope the results also can expand the Sb based anode material family.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqQUrzEtgymvrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhf885ZkxUsNQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhtVags7nN&amp;md5=6e34b0d48afed2593cd6f95a6751d7e4</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref26"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref26'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">26</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit26" data-doi="10.1021/jp507116t"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dai, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bao, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">An SbOx/Reduced Graphene Oxide Composite as a High-Rate Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">An SbOx/Reduced Graphene Oxide Composite as a High-Rate Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhou, Xiaosi; Liu, Xia; Xu, Yan; Liu, Yunxia; Dai, Zhihui; Bao, Jianchun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Physical Chemistry C</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">118</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Antimony has attracted enormous attention as anode materials for sodium-ion batteries owing to its high theor. gravimetric capacity (∼660 mA h g-1).  Despite the outstanding gravimetric capacity advantage, antimony suffers from unsatisfactory electrochem. performance originating from its huge vol. changes during repeated sodium insertion/extn.  Herein, we synthesize an SbOx/reduced graphene oxide (SbOx/RGO) composite through a wet-milling approach accompanied by redox reaction between Sb and GO.  When used as an anode material for sodium-ion batteries, SbOx/RGO exhibits high rate capability and stable cycling performance.  A reversible capacity of 352 mA h g-1 was obtained even at a c.d. of 5 A g-1.  More than 95% capacity retention (409 mA h g-1) was achieved after 100 cycles at a c.d. of 1 A g-1.  The excellent electrochem. performance is due to the Sb-O bonding between nanometer-sized SbOx particles surface and highly conductive RGO, which can not only effectively prevent SbOx nanoparticles from aggregation upon cycling but also promote the electrons and sodium ions transportation.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqnwzPJQle5UrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhf885ZkxUsNQ"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit29R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">29</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Core-Shell Ge@graphene@TiO2 Nanofibers as a High-Capacity and Cycle-Stable Anode for Lithium and Sodium Ion Battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Xiaoyan; Fan, Ling; Gong, Decai; Zhu, Jian; Zhang, Qingfeng; Lu, Bingan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Ge is considered as a promising anode material because of its comparable Li and Na storage capability, but it usually exhibits poor cycling stability due to the large vol. variation during Li or Na uptake and release processes.  Ge@graphene nanofibers are 1st obtained through electrospinning followed by calcination.  Then at. layer deposition is used to fabricate Ge@graphene@TiO2 core-shell nanofibers (Ge@G@TiO2 NFs) as anode materials for Li and Na ion batteries (LIBs and SIBs).  Graphene and TiO2 can double protect the Ge nanofibers in charge and discharge processes.  The Ge@G@TiO2 NFs composite as an anode material is versatile and exhibits enhanced electrochem. performance for LIBs and SIBs.  The capacity of the Ge@G@TiO2 NFs composite can be maintained at 1050 mA h g-1 (100th cycle) and 182 mA h g-1 (250th cycle) for LIBs and SIBs, resp., at a c.d. of 100 mA g-1, showing high capacity and good cycling stability (much better than that of Ge nanofibers or Ge@G nanofibers).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoHe_VK0GTeirVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhf885ZkxUsNQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xpt1Cj&amp;md5=627ef8fad9d57c6a7956ca9c69188753</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref30'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit30" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201403648"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yue, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yingjian, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shibo, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Binbin, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wei, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Binbin, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mingsen Zheng, S.                         cas_cit30R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">30</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High Performance 3D Si/Ge Nanorods Array Anode Buffered by TiN/Ti Interlayer for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yue, Chuang; Yu, Yingjian; Sun, Shibo; He, Xu; Chen, Binbin; Lin, Wei; Xu, Binbin; Zheng, Mingsen; Wu, Suntao; Li, Jing; Kang, Junyong; Lin, Liwei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">3D micro/nanobatteries in high energy and power densities are drawing more and more interest due to the urgent demand of them in integrating with numerous micro/nanoscale electronic devices, such as smart dust, miniaturized sensors, actuators, BioMEMS chips, and so on.  In this study, the electrochem. performances of 3D hexagonal match-like Si/Ge nanorod (NR) arrays buffered by TiN/Ti interlayer, which are fabricated on Si substrates by a cost-effective, wafer scale, and Si-compatible process are demonstrated and systematically investigated as the anode in sodium-ion batteries.  The optimized Si/TiN/Ti/Ge composite NR array anode displays superior areal/specific capacities and cycling stability by reason of their favorable 3D nanostructures and the effective conductive layers of TiN/Ti thin films.  Sodium-ion insertion behaviors are exptl. investigated in postmorphologies and elemental information of the cycled composite anode, and theor. studied by the first principles calcn. upon the adsorption and diffusion energies of sodium in Ge unit cell.  The preferential diffusion of sodium in Ge structure over in Si lattice is evidently proved.  The successful configuration of these distinctive wafer-scale Si-based Na-ion micro/nanobattery anodes can provide insight into exploring and designing new Si/Ge-based electrode materials, which can be integrated into micro-electronic devices as on chip power systems in the future.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpvy2j0ZbDFXrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgpLOluApsWOA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXosFKktA%253D%253D&amp;md5=b50357ed97041d5386333e81d75c8574</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref31"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref31'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">31</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit31" data-doi="10.1016/j.jallcom.2016.07.201"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jung, S.                         cas_cit31R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">31</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Advantages of Ge anode for Na-ion batteries: Ge vs. Si and Sn</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jung, Sung Chul; Kim, Hyung-Jin; Kang, Yong-Ju; Han, Young-Kyu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Alloys and Compounds</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The sodiation properties of alloy-type anode materials (Si, Ge, and Sn) were evaluated in terms of electrochem. energy storage using first-principles mol. dynamics calcns.  It is reported that Ge can deliver reasonably good performance in all aspects of sodium storage capability, mech. stability, and ion cond., when compared with Si and Sn.  The Ge anode has a strong thermodn. driving force for sodiation that is comparable to that of Sn and much stronger than that of Si, exhibits moderate vol. expansion and bulk modulus upon sodiation that are superior to those of Sn, and allows fast Na ion cond. that is comparable to that of Sn and is faster by three orders of magnitude than that of Si.  The study suggests that among the group 14 elements, Ge is fairly promising as an anode material for Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrNj1a61Qy2MbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgpLOluApsWOA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xht1Grsr%252FP&amp;md5=4ef2db25ab7de15efbc78c2994fda82a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit32" data-doi="10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b05081"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chang, W.-C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tseng, K.-W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tuan, H.-Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Solution Synthesis of Iodine-Doped Red Phosphorus Nanoparticles for Lithium-Ion Battery Anodes</span>. <i>Nano Lett.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>17</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1240</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">1247</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Solution Synthesis of Iodine-Doped Red Phosphorus Nanoparticles for Lithium-Ion Battery Anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chang, Wei-Chung; Tseng, Kuan-Wei; Tuan, Hsing-Yu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">17</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1240-1247</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Red phosphorus (RP) is a promising anode material for lithium-ion batteries due to its earth abundance and a high theor. capacity of 2596 mA h g-1.  Although RP-based anodes for lithium-ion batteries have been reported, they were all in the form of carbon-P composites, including P-graphene, P-graphite, P-carbon nanotubes (CNTs), and P-carbon black, to improve P's extremely low cond. and large vol. change during cycling process.  Here, we report the large-scale synthesis of red phosphorus nanoparticles (RPNPs) with sizes ranging from 100 to 200 nm by reacting PI3 with ethylene glycol in the presence of cetyltrimethylammonium bromide (CTAB) in ambient environment.  Unlike the insulator behavior of com. RP (cond. of &lt;10 -12 S m-1), the cond. of RPNPs is between 2.62 × 10-3 and 1.81 × 10-2 S m-1, which is close to that of semiconductor germanium (1.02 × 10-2 S m-1), and 2 orders of magnitude higher than silicon (5.35 × 10-4 S m-1).  Around 3-5 wt % of iodine-doping was found in RPNPs, which was speculated as the key to significantly improve the cond. of RPNPs.  The significantly improved cond. of RPNPs and their uniform colloidal nanostructures enable them to be used solely as active materials for LIBs anodes.  The RPNPs electrodes exhibit a high specific capacity of 1700 mA h g-1 (0.2 C after 100 cycles, 1 C = 2000 mA g-1), long cycling life (∼900 mA h g-1 after 500 cycles at 1 C), and outstanding rate capability (175 mA h g-1 at the charge c.d. of 120 A g-1, 60 C).  Moreover, as a proof-of-concept example, pouch-type full cells using RPNPs anodes and Li(Ni0.5Co0.3Mn0.2)O2 (NCM-532) cathodes were assembled to show their practical uses.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqZ2BwgPjhTMrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgpLOluApsWOA"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A phosphorus/N-doped carbon nanofiber composite as an anode material for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ruan, Boyang; Wang, Jun; Shi, Dongqi; Xu, Yanfei; Chou, Shulei; Liu, Huakun; Wang, Jiazhao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have been attracting intensive attention at present as the most promising alternative to lithium-ion batteries in large-scale elec. energy storage applications, due to the low-cost and natural abundance of sodium.  Elemental phosphorus (P) is a very promising anode material for SIBs, with the highest theor. capacity of 2596 mA h g-1.  Recently, there have been many efforts devoted to phosphorus anode materials for SIBs.  As pure red phosphorus cannot react with Na reversibly, many attempts to prep. composite materials contg. phosphorus have been reported.  Here, we report the facile prepn. of a red phosphorus/N-doped carbon nanofiber composite (P/NCF) that can deliver a reversible capacity of 731 mA h g-1 in sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), with a capacity retention of 57.3% over 55 cycles.                         cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">In Situ Binding Sb Nanospheres on Graphene via Oxygen Bonds as Superior Anode for Ultrafast Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wan, Fang; Guo, Jin-Zhi; Zhang, Xiao-Hua; Zhang, Jing-Ping; Sun, Hai-Zhu; Yan, Qingyu; Han, Dong-Xue; Niu, Li; Wu, Xing-Long</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">7790-7799</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Graphene incorporation should be one effective strategy to develop advanced electrode materials for a sodium-ion battery (SIB).  Herein, the micro/nanostructural Sb/graphene composite (Sb-O-G) is successfully prepd. with the uniform Sb nanospheres (∼100 nm) bound on the graphene via oxygen bonds.  It is revealed that the in-situ-constructed oxygen bonds play a significant role on enhancing Na-storage properties, esp. the ultrafast charge/discharge capability.  The oxygen-bond-enhanced Sb-O-G composite can deliver a high capacity of 220 mAh/g at an ultrahigh c.d. of 12 A/g, which is obviously superior to the similar Sb/G composite (130 mAh/g at 10 A/g) just without Sb-O-C bonds.  It also exhibits the highest Na-storage capacity compared to Sb/G and pure Sb nanoparticles as well as the best cycling performance.  More importantly, this Sb-O-G anode achieves ultrafast (120 C) energy storage in SIB full cells, which have already been shown to power a 26-bulb array and calculator.  All of these superior performances originate from the structural stability of Sb-O-C bonds during Na uptake/release, which has been verified by ex situ X-ray photoelectron spectroscopies and IR spectroscopies.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqAWqDAYuZl6rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljtro6z3MoSdA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XjvFylur8%253D&amp;md5=20ff4444ec296955ad0cbb06a02dfbef</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref37"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref37'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">37</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit37" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2016.06.031"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lim, C.                         cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Experimental Study on Sodiation of Amorphous Silicon for Use as Sodium-Ion Battery Anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lim, Chek-Hai; Huang, Tzu-Yang; Shao, Pei-Sian; Chien, Jen-Hao; Weng, Yu-Ting; Huang, Hsin-Fu; Hwang, Bing Joe; Wu, Nae-Lih</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Amorphous Si (a-Si) powders were synthesized using various synthetic methods, and their electrochem. sodiation behaviors were studied.  These methods include (1) a chem. delithiation method where Si is 1st lithiated and then delithiated either in an aq. or org. soln., (2) a mech. method where cryst. Si is subjected to high-energy ball milling, and (3) a mech. fusion method where a Si-Sn composite with a Si-Sn at. ratio of 0.94:0.06 was synthesized through high-energy ball milling.  Com. Si monoxide (SiO) also was examd. for comparison.  Facile oxidn. of a-Si encountered in the methods (1) and (2) led to low sodiation capacity and huge 1st-cycle irreversible capacity, similar to those of SiO.  By contrast, the mech. fused Si-Sn composite, which contains a Sn shell that prevents the oxidn. of the partially amorphized Si core, exhibits a max. sodiation capacity of 161 mAh g-1 based on active material.  This is translated to an estd. sodiation capacity of ≤230 mAh g-1 for the a-Si component in the composite.  The presence of the Sn shell considerably reduces the 1st-cycle irreversible capacity and charge-transfer resistance, resulting in improved rate and cycle performance.  This suggests a new material design strategy that may enable the use of the a-Si for Na-ion battery anode applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrsrGCViVMVBLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljtro6z3MoSdA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhtVGiu7vM&amp;md5=62fdb9d37f75cf893d88153ec30d7648</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref38'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit38" data-doi="10.1149/2.080403jes"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ellis, L.                         cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">In situ XRD study of silicon, lead and bismuth negative electrodes in nonaqueous sodium cells</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ellis, L.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The electrochem. alloying of sodium with silicon, lead and bismuth was studied by in-situ X-ray diffraction.  No evidence was found for sodium insertion into silicon at temps. up to 60°C.  Lead was found to catalytically decomp. electrolyte, hindering sodiation.  This could be avoided by applying a high current pulse to the cell to sodiate the lead surface.  Once the surface was sodiated, further sodiation of lead could proceed at low currents.  The sodiation of lead followed a path that differs from the equil. phase diagram and from that described in earlier reports.  During sodiation, Na9Pb4 was formed with a previously unreported structure that was found to be isostructural with Na9Sn4.  It was found that Na could be reversibly inserted into bismuth.  The mechanism for bismuth sodiation follows equil. phase behavior.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo0vCh28j3qI7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljtro6z3MoSdA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXkt1Wqtrk%253D&amp;md5=6ed3a505ee165bd021448dca8d6c552b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref39"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref39'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">39</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit39" data-doi="10.1039/c3ee40811f"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hong, S.                         cas_cit39R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">39</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Charge carriers in rechargeable batteries: Na ions vs. Li ions</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hong, Sung You; Kim, Youngjin; Park, Yuwon; Choi, Aram; Choi, Nam-Soon; Lee, Kyu Tae</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2067-2081</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EESNBY</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1754-5706</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  We discuss the similarities and dissimilarities of sodium- and lithium-ion batteries in terms of neg. and pos. electrodes.  Compared to the comprehensive body of work on lithium-ion batteries, research on sodium-ion batteries is still at the germination stage.  Since both sodium and lithium are alkali metals, they share similar chem. properties including ionicity, electronegativity and electrochem. reactivity.  They accordingly have comparable synthetic protocols and electrochem. performances, which indicates that sodium-ion batteries can be successfully developed based on previously applied approaches or methods in the lithium counterpart.  The electrode materials in Li-ion batteries provide the best library for research on Na-ion batteries because many Na-ion insertion hosts have their roots in Li-ion insertion hosts.  However, the larger size and different bonding characteristics of sodium ions influence the thermodn. and/or kinetic properties of sodium-ion batteries, which leads to unexpected behavior in electrochem. performance and reaction mechanism, compared to lithium-ion batteries.  This perspective provides a comparative overview of the major developments in the area of pos. and neg. electrode materials in both Li-ion and Na-ion batteries in the past decade.  Highlighted are concepts in solid state chem. and electrochem. that have provided new opportunities for tailored design that can be extended to many different electrode materials for sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqHBS0wIkomorVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljtro6z3MoSdA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhtVWmtL%252FE&amp;md5=023136cc0e5ed94e18ce0d526a0000a4</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref40"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref40'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">40</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit40" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2013.01.083"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Baggetto, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ganesh, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Meisner, R.                         cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Characterization of sodium ion electrochemical reaction with tin anodes: Experiment and theory</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Baggetto, Loic; Ganesh, P.; Meisner, Roberta P.; Unocic, Raymond R.; Jumas, Jean-Claude; Bridges, Craig A.; Veith, Gabriel M.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sn anodes show a rich structure and reaction chem. which the authors have studied.  Upon discharge five plateaus are obsd. corresponding to β-Sn, an unidentified phase (Na/Sn = 0.6), an amorphous phase (Na/Sn = 1.2), a hexagonal R-3m Na5Sn2, and fully sodiated I-43d Na15Sn4.  With charging there are six plateaus related to the formation of Na5Sn2 followed by the formation of amorphous phases and β-Sn.  Upon cycling the formation of metastable Na5Sn2 seems to be suppressed.  Theor. voltages calcd. from existing crystal structures using DFT provide a good match with const. current and quasi-equil. measurements (GITT).  Search for addnl. (meta)stable phases using cluster-expansion method predicts many phases lower in energy than the convex hull obtained from known structures, including the R-3m Na5Sn2 phase.  The presence of multiple phases in varying lattices with similar formation energy suggests why the reaction mechanism is nonreversible. 119Sn Mossbauer spectroscopy results indicate a decrease of the isomer shift with increasing Na/Sn content, which is less pronounced than for Li-Sn compds. likely due to the lower electropositivity of Na.  The electrode surface is terminated with an SEI layer rich in carbonates (Na2CO3 and Na CO3R) as evidenced by XPS.  After charge at 2 V, strong evidence for the formation of oxidized Sn4+ was obtained.  Subjecting the electrode to a rest after charge at 2 V reveals that aging in the electrolyte reduces the oxidized Sn4+ into Sn2+ and Sn0, and concomitantly suppresses the electrolyte decompn. represented by an anomalous discharge plateau at 1.2 V.  Thereby, the catalytic decompn. of the electrolyte during discharge is caused by nanosized Sn particles covered by oxidized Sn4+ and not by pure metallic Sn.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpyrhOO554AnLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljZX-PVQbS9vg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXktFOktb0%253D&amp;md5=5bd2e34aea41e7840c8666db62bf7efe</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref41"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref41'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">41</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit41" data-doi="10.1039/C5EE02524A"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gan, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ke, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhai, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Layered Phosphorus-Like GeP5: a Promising Anode Candidate with High Initial Coulombic Efficiency and Large Capacity for lithium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Energy Environ.                         cas_cit41R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">41</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Layered phosphorus-like GeP5: a promising anode candidate with high initial coulombic efficiency and large capacity for lithium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Wenwu; Li, Huiqiao; Lu, Zhijuan; Gan, Lin; Ke, Linbo; Zhai, Tianyou; Zhou, Haoshen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3629-3636</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">In this work, we for the first time investigate GeP5 as an anode material for lithium ion batteries (LIBs).  Using a facile high energy mech. ball milling (HEMM) method, we successfully synthesize pure GeP5 and GeP5/C nanocomposite at ambient temp. and pressure.  According to XRD Rietveld refinement and first principle calcns., GeP5 possesses a two-dimensional layered structure similar to that of black P and graphite, and a high cond. that is 10 000 and 10 times that of black P and graphite, resp.  Serving as novel anode materials, both GeP5 and its carbon composite deliver an unprecedented high reversible capacity of ca. 2300 mA h g-1, combined with a high initial coulombic efficiency of ca. 95%.  Ex situ XRD and CV tests demonstrate that GeP5 undergoes conversion and alloying type lithium storage mechanism and that its capacity is co-contributed to by both the Ge and P components.  In addn., GeP5/C exhibits superior cycle stability and excellent high-rate performance with a capacity of 2127 mA h g-1 at 5 A g-1.  These properties suggest the promising application of these anode materials in next-generation high-energy and high-power LIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo42mASYGbNzrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljZX-PVQbS9vg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhs1Sit7rI&amp;md5=12cb34ee45b760a90c13b77874416545</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref42"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref42'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">42</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit42" data-doi="10.1039/C7TA00139H"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ke, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wei, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gan, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhai, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Highly Reversible Sodium Storage in a GeP5/C Composite Anode with Large Capacity and Low Voltage</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit42R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">42</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Highly reversible sodium storage in a GeP5/C composite anode with large capacity and low voltage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Wenwu; Ke, Linbo; Wei, Yaqing; Guo, Shaohua; Gan, Lin; Li, Huiqiao; Zhai, Tianyou; Zhou, Haoshen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium ion batteries (SIBs) are considered to be a promising alternative to lithium ion batteries because of the high abundance of sodium.  However, the scarcities of suitable anode materials severely hamper the development of SIBs.  Here, we synthesized a GeP5/C composite with binary sodium-reactive components on a large scale.  Theor., it can promise a capacity of 1888 mA h g-1 or 6891 mA h cm-3, which is the best record in anodes for SIBs reported so far.  In practice, the GeP5/C showed a low potential of ≈0.4 V vs.  Na+/Na with a smooth charge/discharge profile.  It delivered a large reversible capacity of 1250 mA h g-1 with a first coulombic efficiency of 93%.  Electrochem.-mechanism studies suggested that the formation of a GeP5 phase endowed a high first coulombic efficiency and synergetic effect between the sodiation of Ge and P.  This effect smoothly leveled the multistep plateaus and effectively reduced the polarization between charge/discharge.  When applied to a full cell by coupling a Na3V2(PO4)3/C cathode, the assembled Na3V2(PO4)3//GeP5 full cell showed a large capacity of 800 mA h g-1 with a high av. output voltage of 2.65 V.                         cas_cit43R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">43</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">GeP5/C composite as anode material for high power sodium-ion batteries with exceptional capacity</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Yujie; Xiao, Xuezhang; Fan, Xiulin; Li, Meng; Zhang, Yiwen; Zhang, Wei; Chen, Lixin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Alloys and Compounds</span>

                        cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Extended photocurrent performance of antimony trisulfide/reduced graphene oxide composite prepared via a facile hot-injection route</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Molaei, Pezhman; Kazeminezhad, Iraj</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Ceramics International</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">44</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Antimony trisulfide/reduced graphene oxide (Sb2S3-rGO) composite was successfully prepd. via a facile hot-injection route at a relatively low temp. using ethylene glycol (EG) as a nontoxic and cost-effective solvent.  The phase, structure, and characteristic properties of the products were examd. by X-ray powder diffraction (XRD), Fourier transform IR spectroscopy (FTIR), Raman spectroscopy, field emission SEM (FESEM), energy-dispersive X-ray spectroscopy (EDS), and UV-vis spectroscopy.  The results revealed that growth of Sb2S3 nanorods on rGO occurred with a single phase and av. diam. of 50 nm.  An optimum temp. of 150 °C was confirmed for the synthesis of Sb2S3-rGO using the hot-injection method.  Furthermore, electrochem. impedance spectroscopy (EIS) measurement revealed an excellent redn. in charge transfer resistance (RCT) of Sb2S3-rGO layer that is about 20 times smaller than that of Sb2S3, indicating an obvious increase in charge transport and redn. in recombination rate.  Also, compare to Sb2S3, the transient photocurrent response of Sb2S3-rGO layer was sharply enhanced by a factor of 6 probably because of the excellent elec. cond. of rGO in Sb2S3-rGO composite layer.  These results strongly suggest Sb2S3-rGO composite as an earth-abundant compd. in solar cell applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq0XjxvD0oterVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljZX-PVQbS9vg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXot1Gitb4%253D&amp;md5=51a8870851ffefc5189e61629b08e7d3</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref46'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit46" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.7b00557"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lau, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, T.                 10.1021/acsnano.7b00557</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D11%26publication_year%3D2017%26pages%3D5530-5537%26journal%3DACS%2BNano%26author%3DY.%2BLiu%26author%3DA.%2BZhang%26author%3DC.%2BShen%26author%3DQ.%2BLiu%26author%3DX.%2BCao%26author%3DY.%2BMa%26author%3DL.%2BChen%26author%3DC.%2BLau%26author%3DT.%2BC.%2BChen%26author%3DF.%2BWei%26author%3DC.%2BZhou%26title%3DRed%2BPhosphorus%2BNanodots%2Bon%2BReduced%2BGraphene%2BOxide%2Bas%2Ba%2BFlexible%2Band%2BUltra-Fast%2BAnode%2Bfor%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facsnano.7b00557&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.8b11103&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facsnano.7b00557&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit46R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">46</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Red Phosphorus Nanodots on Reduced Graphene Oxide as a Flexible and Ultra-Fast Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Yihang; Zhang, Anyi; Shen, Chenfei; Liu, Qingzhou; Cao, Xuan; Ma, Yuqiang; Chen, Liang; Lau, Christian; Chen, Tian-Chi; Wei, Fei; Zhou, Chongwu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">11</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5530-5537</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries offer an attractive option for potential low cost and large scale energy storage due to the earth abundance of Na.  Red P is considered as a high capacity anode for Na-ion batteries with a theor. capacity of 2596 mA-h/g.  However, similar to Si in Li-ion batteries, several limitations, such as large vol. expansion upon sodiation/desodiation and low electronic conductance, have limited the performance of red P anodes.  To address the above challenges, the authors have developed a method to deposit red P nanodots densely and uniformly onto reduced graphene oxide sheets (P@RGO) to minimize the Na ion diffusion length and the sodiation/desodiation stresses, and the RGO network also serves as electron pathway and creates free space to accommodate the vol. variation of P particles.  The resulted P@RGO flexible anode achieved 1165.4, 510.6, and 135.3 mA-h/g specific charge capacity at 159.4, 31878.9, and 47818.3 mA/g charge/discharge c.d. in rate capability test, and a 914 mA-h/g capacity after 300 deep cycles in cycling stability test at 1593.9 mA/g c.d., which marks a significant performance improvement for red P anodes for Na-ion chem. and flexible power sources for wearable electronics.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo9mlp0D8us-rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhKJ9q8Y5WKmA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXot1ygtr8%253D&amp;md5=33417000c419534df3b536cd70b89933</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref47"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref47'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">47</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit47" data-doi="10.1021/nl403053v"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, W. Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, H. K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dou, S. X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Simply Mixed Commercial Red Phosphorus and Carbon Nanotube Composite with Exceptionally Reversible Sodium-Ion Storage</span>. <i>Nano Lett.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2013</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>13</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">5480</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">5484</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/nl403053v</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D13%26publication_year%3D2013%26pages%3D5480-5484%26journal%3DNano%2BLett.%26author%3DW.%2BJ.%2BLi%26author%3DS.%2BL.%2BChou%26author%3DJ.%2BZ.%2BWang%26author%3DH.%2BK.%2BLiu%26author%3DS.%2BX.%2BDou%26title%3DSimply%2BMixed%2BCommercial%2BRed%2BPhosphorus%2Band%2BCarbon%2BNanotube%2BComposite%2Bwith%2BExceptionally%2BReversible%2BSodium-Ion%2BStorage%26doi%3D10.1021%252Fnl403053v&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.8b11103&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Fnl403053v&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit47R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">47</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Simply mixed commercial red phosphorus and carbon nanotube composite with exceptionally reversible sodium-ion storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Wei-Jie; Chou, Shu-Lei; Wang, Jia-Zhao; Liu, Hua-Kun; Dou, Shi-Xue</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">13</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5480-5484</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NALEFD</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1530-6984</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Recently, sodium ion batteries (SIBs) have been given intense attention because they are the most promising alternative to lithium ion batteries for application in renewable power stations and smart grid, owing to their low cost, their abundant natural resources, and the similar chem. of sodium and lithium.  Elemental phosphorus (P) is the most promising anode materials for SIBs with the highest theor. capacity of 2596 mA h g-1, but the com. available red phosphorus cannot react with Na reversibly.  Here, we report that simply hand-grinding com. microsized red phosphorus and carbon nanotubes (CNTs) can deliver a reversible capacity of 1675 mA h g-1 for sodium ion batteries (SIBs), with capacity retention of 76.6% over 10 cycles.  Our results suggest that the simply mixed com. red phosphorus and CNTs would be a promising anode candidate for SIBs with a high capacity and low cost.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoXaIaGjScJ9bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhKJ9q8Y5WKmA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhslSgtb7F&amp;md5=0d930b4524af251e6376a18cb67d5e91</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref48"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref48'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">48</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit48" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2017.08.019"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Song, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, D.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Advanced Anode for Sodium-ion Battery with Promising Long Cycling Stability Achieved by Tuning Phosphorus-Carbon Nanostructures</span>. <i>Nano Energy</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>40</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">550</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">558</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.nanoen.2017.08.019</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D40%26publication_year%3D2017%26pages%3D550-558%26journal%3DNano%2BEnergy%26author%3DZ.%2BYu%26author%3DJ.%2BSong%26author%3DD.%2BWang%26author%3DD.%2BWang%26title%3DAdvanced%2BAnode%2Bfor%2BSodium-ion%2BBattery%2Bwith%2BPromising%2BLong%2BCycling%2BStability%2BAchieved%2Bby%2BTuning%2BPhosphorus-Carbon%2BNanostructures%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.nanoen.2017.08.019&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.8b11103&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.nanoen.2017.08.019&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit48R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">48</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Advanced anode for sodium-ion battery with promising long cycling stability achieved by tuning phosphorus-carbon nanostructures</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yu, Zhaoxin; Song, Jiangxuan; Wang, Daiwei; Wang, Donghai</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">40</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">550-558</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NEANCA</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2211-2855</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Phosphorus is considered as a promising anode for Na-ion battery because of its high theor. capacity of 2595 mAh g-1.  In this study, two phosphorus-carbon (P-C) composites with well-controlled compns. and nanostructures of P and C have been developed: P@YP composite with P confined within porous structure of YP-80F carbon and P@CNT with unconfined P deposited on the surface of carbon nanotube.  The structure and electrochem. performance of these two composites have been studied to illustrate the effect of nanostructures of both C and P.  P@YP composite with appropriate amt. of P confined in nanopores can accommodate its large vol. change upon sodiation/desodiation and enable a stable solid-electrolyte interphase (SEI), ensuring an excellent long-term cycling stability with superior capacity retention of 92% after 100 cycles and 46% after 1000 cycles.  In contrast, the P@CNT composite with unconfined P nanostructures shows a rapid capacity decay with capacity retention of ∼ 40.6% after 100 cycles, most likely due to unstable SEI during cycling, caused by the large vol. changes of unconfined P in the P@CNT composite.  The well-designed nanostructured P-C composite with P confined within porous structure of carbon is demonstrated to greatly enhance the electrochem. performance, leading to promising long-term cycling stability.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrzjZhB2uHFi7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhKJ9q8Y5WKmA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhsVOjt77N&amp;md5=3d3a2e634df272a1655713bea63694f8</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref49"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref49'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">49</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit49" data-doi="10.1038/ncomms12122"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chao, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xia, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fan, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Savilov, S.                         cas_cit49R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">49</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Array of nanosheets render ultrafast and high-capacity Na-ion storage by tunable pseudocapacitance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chao, Dongliang; Zhu, Changrong; Yang, Peihua; Xia, Xinhui; Liu, Jilei; Wang, Jin; Fan, Xiaofeng; Savilov, Serguei V.; Lin, Jianyi; Fan, Hong Jin; Shen, Ze Xiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">12122</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NCAOBW</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2041-1723</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries are a potentially low-cost and safe alternative to the prevailing lithium-ion battery technol.  However, it is a great challenge to achieve fast charging and high power d. for most sodium-ion electrodes because of the sluggish sodiation kinetics.  Here we demonstrate a high-capacity and high-rate sodium-ion anode based on ultrathin layered tin(II) sulfide nanostructures, in which a maximized extrinsic pseudocapacitance contribution is identified and verified by kinetics anal.  The graphene foam supported tin(II) sulfide nanoarray anode delivers a high reversible capacity of ∼1,100 mAh g-1 at 30 mA g-1 and ∼420 mAh g-1 at 30 A g-1, which even outperforms its lithium-ion storage performance.  The surface-dominated redox reaction rendered by our tailored ultrathin tin(II) sulfide nanostructures may also work in other layered materials for high-performance sodium-ion storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrVSw-KQ43s-LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhKJ9q8Y5WKmA"> &gt;&gt;
